0:40  His speech was hindered by his English, his use of metaphors became confusing but I believe his speech has a good meaning behind it, my interpretation is this:    "As flies to want boys. We are for the goat, they kill us for the sport"   As flies ( the football players, managers, etc.)  to want boys (Referring to youths, the younger generation that will make and replace the older generation in the future)   We are for the goat (I'm assuming he said, we are for the Greatest Of All Time, GOAT or it was probably a metaphor which I didn't pick up)  They kill us for the sport (I"m assuming the "they" he's talking about is "aging" due to the next contents of his speech)  "Soon the science will not only be able to slow down the aging of the cells, soon the science will be, will fix the cells."  This whole sentence refers to, in the future,  science can fix the broken cells that our body can't fix due to aging.   "Soon the science will be, will fix the cells to that state and so we'd become, eternal."   Once science can fix the cells and return them to their original state then we'd become eternal. I'm interpreting his sentence in 2 ways, since he's speaking in UEFA, eternal as in, playing football eternally.   1. Playing the beautiful sport we call football, eternally.  or  2. Live our lives as humans, eternally and to not worry about aging as our cause of death  That's probably what he meant.   "Only accidents, crimes and wars will multiply."   Since it's possible to live forever because science has fixed the "issue" of aging then accidents, crimes and wars are the only ways of ending a life and they will multiply due to the surplus amount of people living. Since nobody is dying due to aging then death by these events will increase.   "I love football"   It's pretty straightforward.   Anyways, I'm probably looking into this too deeply or something.

Witness: Killing on Demand  Professor Martin Elliott at the hearing on November 29  Martin Elliott, MD FRCS, professor emeritus of cardiothoracic surgery at University College London (UCL), is a member of the China Tribunal. He explained at the hearing some of the evidence that has been evaluated by the Tribunal, including that the number of organ transplants far exceeded the organ donations, the unexplained physical examinations conducted at labor camps, and the short wait times for organ transplants.  Based on scientific publications, hospital websites, and other resources, Canadian human rights lawyer David Matas estimated that organ transplants in China ranged between 60,000 and 90,000 per year, a number much higher than the number of organ donations claimed by China. This discrepancy indicates the existence of a hidden organ donor bank.  In addition, detainees were required to have blood tests and organ ultrasound tests for no apparent reason. Some of the detainees also went missing from labor camps and other detention facilities. Given how these detainees were tortured, it is hard to imagine that such tests were for their health. Furthermore, these blood and ultrasound tests were not documented in routine procedures.  Consistent with the evidence listed above are the short wait times for organs. In most European countries the wait times are usually months or even up to two years. But data showed that wait times in China are often as short as a few days. This can only be explained by a hidden organ donor bank.  Citing calculations from independent journalist Ethan Gutmann, Sir Geoffrey said that each human with usable organs could generate a profit of between $500,000 and $750,000.  Elliott further explained that this is a business model of on-demand supply. In one case, a Japanese citizen needed a new liver and was willing to pay $5 million for it through an agent. The agent contacted a hospital in China and secured a transplant facility in a short time with the organ needed. Sometimes, spare organs were also available. Such a business model is unimaginable in Western countries.  He emphasized that when talking about China, he was referring to the CCP and its policies, not Chinese citizens.

Yoo
For anyone wondering what Cantona meant: "As flies to wanton boys we are to the gods. They kill us for the sport ".  It is likely that with these words Cantona is criticizing the political class (the Gods in this metaphor) in football (UEFA and FIFA). The flies are the players, starting with Leo Messi and Cristiano Ronaldo. For Cantona the players do not have sufficient power and strength, those in charge will continue to have control of the game for their interests.   "Soon the science will not only be able to slow down the aging of the cells; soon the science will fix the cells to the state. And so we become eternal"  This passage, which seems to lighten the tones, can be understood in two ways. The first is the more scientific one, which criticizes the new figure of the athlete and a game that depends more and more on the physical component (meanwhile CR7 does not smile). The second interpretation is the more political and controversial one, addressed once again to the federal bodies. The cells would be the metaphor of the goals of the state, made eternal and unassailable by technology, which represses the freedom, imagination and spontaneity of football. The play on words and the double meaning of the English term "State" (State), could justify this way of seeing the thing.

However, with scientific advancements like de-aging arriving, sooner or later everyone is going to have the ability to live forever. So how can you judge who is the GOAT if longevity is no longer a factor, and every great player stays great because they don't age? So, enjoy the sports and the GOATS that come along with it as much as you can, because what makes sports great will soon be killed by science. And the unfortunate side to that is that because everyone now has de-aging ability, only incidents like accidents, wars, and crimes can take away a human's life. So, if we hear about the end of a GOAT's career, it's not because they retired, it's cuz they're dead.
